If PATH would be NP-complete, this would, by deﬁnition, imply that for all
L ∈NP, L ≤P PATH. But this again implies that for all L in NP, L is in P. Thus
P = NP would follow, which we (except maybe some cranks) believe is not true.
We show that proving that PATH is not NP-complete implies that NP=P. We 6
show this by contraposition: we assume P=NP and then show that PATH is
NP-complete: so assume P=NP. Using exercise 7.17 it then follows that PATH
is NP-complete. Thus if PATH is not NP-complete, it should be the case that
NP=P, which is what we wanted to prove

1: k   number of states of G
2: if k = 2 then
3: Return (s, a)
4: else
5: Select any state qrip 2 Q − {s, a}
6: Q′   Q − {qrip}
7: for all qi 2 Q − {a} do
8: for all qj 2 Q − {s} do
9: R1   (qi, qrip)
10: R2   (qrip, qrip)
11: R3   (qrip, qj)
12: R4   (qi, qj)
13: ′(qi, qj)   [(R1)(R2)∗(R3)] [ (R4)
14: G′   (Q′,, ′, s, a)

bas every P is in NP obvs! bas till now we're not sure if its the other way around..so when u say that A<=p B ..n u know that A is in P then ofcourse we can reduce it to sumn which is in NP and we can also reduce it to sumn which is in P "i suppose" ..which means that B can either be in NP or P so knowing that A is in P doesnt tell us anything bout B, however if A is NP we know for sure that B has to be in NP cuz if it were in P then we'd prove that NP = P :D

12990 - Mohamed El Menisy: Closure properties

Context-free languages are closed under several common operations.

Union
Suppose we have grammars for two languages, with start symbols S and T. Rename variables as needed to ensure that the two grammars don't share any variables. Then construct a grammar for the union of the languages, with start symbol Z, by taking all the rules from both grammars and adding a new rule Z -> S | T.
Concatenation
Suppose we have grammars for two languages, with start symbols S and T. Rename variables as needed to ensure that the two grammars don't share any variables. Then construct a grammar for the union of the languages, with start symbol Z, by taking all the rules from both grammars and adding a new rule Z -> ST.
Star
Suppose that we have a grammar for the language L, with start symbol S. The grammar for L*, with start symbol T, contains all the rules from the original grammar plus the rule T -> TS | ε.
String reversal
Reverse the character string on the righthand side of every rule in the grammar.

 A is the primary key and
 B -> C is a functional dependency.

 Decomposition (lossless) into:
R1(B,C) with a primary key B.
 R2(A,B) with a primary key A and foreign key B.

13811 - Mohamed El Menisy: wiki

The care-of address can be acquired by the mobile node in two different ways:
Foreign agent care-of address (FACoA): The mobile node receives the same CoA as the foreign agent. All mobile nodes in the foreign network are given the same CoA.
Co-located care-of address: Each mobile node in the foreign network is assigned its own CoA, usually by a DHCP server. This might happen in a network where the foreign agent has not been deployed yet.

14452 - Jolly Salah: Simbaa Simbaaa How u doiinnnnn ?!!! :D :D


As for the other parts of the 3D topic, observe your environment and ask yourself the following questions:
• How could this chair, table, monitor etc. be modelled in 3D?
• What type of mapping/texture should be used to provide the object with a realistic surface?
• Where should which type of light be placed to reach a special atmosphere in the image? (for this aspect, you can observe and analyse pictures, news programs and movies)


3AIZIN EGABA MO7TARAMA LEL SO2AL DA  !! :D  ... ETSARRAF ! 8-|

14453 - Mohamed El Menisy: :D :D ana kont sakket kol dah 3ashan teshofi ad eh Simba mottee3 >_<
howa "Noon el ga3m" dih beta3ood 3ala meen?! :D :p
tyb el chair masalan is gona be modeled by combining different parts together..for example the legs could be modeled by direct extrusion of squares n the same for the "seat" part and the back can also be modeled by extruding a rectangle..these pieces could then be assembled together n grouped to form one object..we can use diffuse mapping by obtaining a 2D image of a wooden surface and map it to the chair to give it the look and feel of wood..we can also specify some degree of shininess to the chair's surface to give a galvanized look!
The ambient light used should not be too strong or we would lose contrast..15,15,15 seems like a good value of it, we can also use an omni light with the source being at the top of the scene to give the effect of a light bulb light that is coming from the ceiling. spot lights over certain objects can be also used to emphasize the importance of these objects in the scene with respect to other objects.

14474 - Jolly Salah: PAL Video rate = 25 frame / sec 
PAL horizontal resolution = 576 line/frame

How many sample / line ba2a ?? :D

One line consists of 
720 pix (luminance-Y) 
+
360 pix (RED -Y )
+
360 pix (Blue -Y)
=
1440 sample / line
